Chiang Kai-shek Arrives in Hankou 105

Soong Mei-ling Accompanies Him and Visits the Red Cliff While Passing Through Huangzhou

The Ship "Ying Rui" Fires a Salute Upon Landing in Hankou

Hankou Correspondence – Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission and Commander-in-Chief of the Anti-Banditry in the Three Provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, decided on the entire plan for the anti-banditry campaign after the Lushan Conference. At 3:00 PM on the 27th, he descended from Guling and arrived in Xunyang at 5:00 PM. At 6:00 PM, he boarded the military ship "Ying Rui" and went west, accompanied by the military ship "Yong Sui". He Chengjun, the Pacification Director, received the telegram late on the night of the 27th. Early in the morning of the 28th, He, Xia Douyin, Xu Yuanquan, Wei Lihuang, Cao Haosen, Qian Zhuolun, Lu Zuo, Lin Xiang, Chen Xizeng, Zhu Chuanjing, Yang Kuiyi, Chen Guangzu, Ye Peng, Qian Dajun, Zhang Yinxiang, Ma Dengying, Zhang Zhenhan, Rong Jingfang, Tang Enbo, Yu Jishi, Kong Geng, Li Shucheng, and others went to the riverbank to greet him. They also ordered the security battalion of the 88th Division, the security company of the Garrison Brigade, the security team of the Public Security Bureau, the Maritime Public Security Bureau, and the "Mos" planes of the 5th Aviation Squadron to be on alert. The security along the route from the port to the Commander-in-Chief's office and the Yihua Village residence was extremely tight. Chiang's itinerary was that he should arrive in Hankou at 9:00 AM on the 28th, but by 10:00 AM, no telegrams had been received from nearby areas, so a plane was dispatched, piloted by Tian Xi, to inspect the Huangzhou area. According to the report from the returned plane, the "Ying Rui" ship arrived in Huangzhou at 8:00 AM. Chiang ordered the ship to stop and disembarked with Soong Mei-ling to visit the Red Cliff, staying for about two hours. He returned to the ship at about 10:00 AM and continued to sail upstream. At 11:00 AM, he passed through Tuanfeng, and was expected to arrive in Hankou at about 3:00 PM. The Second Fleet of the Navy and the headquarters of the Pacification Headquarters also separately received wireless telegrams from the captain of the "Ying Rui" and Chiang's confidential secretaries Li Wan and Deng Wenyi, who were on the ship, stating that they would arrive in Hankou at 3:00 PM. At 3:00 PM, the "Ying Rui" ship indeed entered the port and docked in the center of the river in front of the Jianghan Customs. The "Yong Sui" followed behind and docked on the Wuchang Xujiapeng river surface. At that time, the military band on the shore played music in unison. He Chengjun, Xia Douyin, and others boarded the "Xiangyun," "Zhenyuan," and "Yuehan No. 2" small steam launches to greet him. Chiang then took a small launch ashore with Soong Mei-ling and the two sons of Kong Xiangxi. The "Ying Rui" ship fired a 19-gun salute to escort him. After Chiang landed, he took a car to the Yihua Village residence and first met with He Chengjun and Xia Douyin for a brief discussion. Chiang will schedule a separate meeting with other personnel later. That night, Chiang summoned Cao Haosen to the residence for a brief discussion and planned to convene a conversation with the generals in Hankou on the 29th. However, because the entire plan has already been determined, it will not be presented in the form of a meeting. Chiang, because he is tired of the noise, plans to move to the new campus of Wuhan University on Luojia Mountain in Wuchang to work. The headquarters will be decided to be located in Hankou. If Chiang moves to Luojia Mountain to work, then it may also be moved to Wuchang, which is uncertain. (June 28)

The Southern Section of the Ping-Han Railway is Still Chaotic 106

Guangshui Tracks Repaired But Destroyed

Liu Zhi Leads Two Divisions South to Supervise the Suppression

Hankou Correspondence – On the 26th of this month, bandit alerts occurred simultaneously in Lujiashan, Dongshuanghe, and Lijiazhai in the southern section of the Ping-Han Railway. On the 27th, the bandits had fled west, and the tracks near Guangshui were quickly repaired. Unexpectedly, they were destroyed again on the 28th. By the evening, they were repaired again. Repairs have not yet begun between Xindian and Liulin. On the 27th and 28th, all northbound scheduled trains went to Guangshui and turned back, and the area further north was even more chaotic. It is heard that the bandit plan was to attack Guangshan and Huangchuan unsuccessfully, so they turned to the railway. They were originally divided into three routes: one attacked Wushengguan, one attacked Lijiazhai, and one attacked Xinyang, intending to completely disrupt the transportation between Henan and Hubei. Later, because the suppression army was quickly mobilized, the bandits did not succeed and only briefly invaded Lijiazhai. Although the extent of the damage to the Ping-Han Railway has not been thoroughly investigated, it can be known that it is no less than five or six places. It is also heard that Jigong Mountain in southern Henan was also disturbed, and ten people who were there to escape the summer heat were kidnapped. Seven of them escaped, but the whereabouts of the remaining three are unknown. Fifteen employees were kidnapped. It was previously reported that five people had escaped, but this has not yet been confirmed. It is also reported that when the bandits destroyed the Ping-Han Railway, two trains were robbed near a station near Lujiashan, resulting in significant losses. The Management Committee of the Ping-Han Railway Bureau received a telegram from the section chief of the Huayuan Station stating that at 6:00 AM on the 28th, he took a handcar to Lujiashan and found that four rails had been removed at 1112 kilometers and 433 meters and discarded in the river. They could be repaired by 10:00 AM this morning. It was also found that the No. 613 locomotive of the No. 610 train and its water tank car were both between 1115 kilometers, Guangshui, and Huayuan and could be opened to traffic. However, the Lujiashan station was completely destroyed, and repairs were more difficult. According to Telegram No. 682 from the Guangshui Transportation Section, the people near Guangshui are extremely panicked. The 66-kilometer mark was destroyed again on the evening of the 27th and urgently needs military assistance. After receiving the telegram, the Road Committee telegraphed the Henan-Hubei-Anhui Bandit Suppression Headquarters and the Hubei Pacification Commissioner's Office, requesting that the incoming troops be ordered to provide immediate assistance to maintain transportation. At the same time, it also telegraphed the Ministry of Railways to report the current situation. The original telegram was roughly divided into four points: (1) The tracks destroyed between Shuanghe and Liulin were repaired on the 26th, and normal traffic was restored. The whereabouts of the four shackmen of 274 shacks are still unknown. (2) The Red Bandits at Lujiashan Station have withdrawn after the 13th Division sent a team to station there. Stationmaster Wang Gongchang and more than ten workers and police officers were kidnapped. The station funds were not robbed. A No. 934 guard car was burned, and many telegraph poles and tracks were cut off. The ticket office and public property were all torn down. There are reactionary slogans all over the station. (3) All the destroyed places in Lujiashan, Huayuan, Yanjiadian, and Weijiadian have been repaired by noon today. Traffic between Hankou and Guangshui has been barely restored. The 2nd Express train has been ordered to return to Hankou. (4) The fighting near Lijiazhai has stopped, and it seems to have shifted towards Xinyang. Bandit traces have been discovered again near Donghuangdian. Some bandits specializing in destruction are still lurking along the railway. Chairman Liu Zhi has been stationed in Minggang to supervise the suppression. The 13th Division under Wan Yaohuang has advanced to Lujiashan, and the 14th Army under Wei Lihuang has also advanced to Donghuangdian to jointly search and suppress the bandits. In order to prevent the bandits from fleeing elsewhere, Ma Hongkui's troops have temporarily prohibited traffic from passing through Xinyang. It will probably take another three or four days for north-south traffic to be smooth. As for the mail from Ping-Han, which could not be delivered, light mail sent to the north of Guangshui on the 26th and 27th was returned by the post office and transferred to ships to Nanjing, and then sent to the Tianjin-Pukou and Longhai lines. (June 28)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang 107

The county government issued a notice to the public about the collection of the first phase of land tax, stating that the first phase of land price tax for the 21st year should be collected from July 1st of this year at the first and second field tax collection offices of the Finance Bureau. Branch offices will be set up in areas far from the city to facilitate tax payment for grain households. For the disaster arrears in each district of the 20th year, permission has been granted for exemption and general reduction. All silver dollars overpaid that year should be allowed to be deducted separately from each map of the first phase of land price tax of this year. The original 5 cents of silver per mu for the security map expenses levied with the 38 insurance maps should be temporarily allowed to continue to be levied for one year this year and should still be ordered to be levied in separate books by the cabinet. The amount of silver to be levied should be checked according to the number listed on the notification form for simple viewing, and tax preparation should be self-sealed and submitted to the cabinet for completion, with August 31st as the deadline, and penalties will be imposed according to regulations if the deadline is exceeded.

The Education Committee of the First District Was Abolished – The county Education Bureau previously received an order from the Education Department to issue revised organization regulations and classification standards and expense expenditure forms for county Education Bureaus and immediately complied with the order. After receiving the order, Director Zhu examined the existing funds in the county and found that the number of education committee members could only be four, and there were six school districts, so two districts should be merged. However, because the county is a merger of the Hua and Lou counties, and the land is vast, if the school districts are merged immediately, obstacles are inevitable in practice. Therefore, it is proposed that the school districts remain the same for the time being, but one education committee member will be reduced. The duties of the education committee member of the first school district in the suburban areas of the city will be handled by the education committee members of the second, third, fourth, fifth, and sixth districts, who will make nearby inspections of the schools in the first school district when they return to the city to be stationed in the bureau during inspection intervals. The administrative affairs of the district will be handled concurrently by the county superintendent, so that the business will not be abandoned and the instructions of the Education Department to tighten the budget will still be followed. It has been submitted to the Education Department for approval and transfer for implementation.

Suzhou 108

Ta Lake Estuary Bandit Alert: Recently, bandits in various villages of Wuxian County have been on the rise, with frequent cases of kidnapping and robbery. On the 27th, six or seven bandit boats were discovered at the Jinshu Village port. The 3rd squad of the police team was dispatched to pursue them, but they fled towards Xiaogong in Tai Lake. Police Captain Du received a telegram from Kong, the district chief of Hengjing, stating that bandits were constantly appearing and disappearing in places like Puzhuang and Shuzhuang, and were even impersonating police to carry out robberies under the guise of bandit suppression. District Chief Kong requested the dispatch of a team to search and suppress the bandits. Captain Du immediately sent the 1st company, led by Captain Zhu, to conduct the search. At the Ta Lake estuary in Puzhuang, eight or nine bandit boats suddenly emerged from the reed thickets. The bandits, numbering over a hundred, immediately opened fire on the police team. After about half an hour of battle, the bandits were defeated and fled towards Tai Lake.

Crackdown on Illegal Coin Minting: At No. 24 Xinqiao Lane, Panmen, Xu Tinghua and others had set up a facility for illegally minting lead coins. This was discovered by the detective team, which dispatched detectives on the 27th to make arrests. They seized a set of molds for casting lead coins, a lead melting pot, seven iron sheet mold edges, twenty-eight counterfeit lead dual mill coins, and lead residue. Xu Tinghua was arrested and confessed, stating that Li Debiao was responsible for selling the lead coins for 25 cents per yuan. They were sent to the Public Security Bureau and transferred to the local court for interrogation.

Wuxi 109

Autopsy in Dang Kou Murder Case: Zou Fugen, an apprentice at Wu Yilong's noodle shop in Dang Kou Town, Nanyan City, was selling fried dough sticks at the Lao Long Yuan teahouse on Wu Wang Bridge when he was beaten by a tea guest named Hua Jin Heshang. He died several days later. The shop owner, Wu Chungen, prepared a coffin and hastily arranged the burial. Hua Chongliang, a citizen of the town, reported the incident to the county court. Prosecutor Du summoned Wu Chungen and others to court for questioning. As a result, court police officers Sun Yun and Chen Liansheng were dispatched, along with Wu Chungen and the map official Jiang Yisheng, to the countryside to transport the coffin to the city for an autopsy. The autopsy was scheduled to take place at the stone archway at the foot of Xishan. On the afternoon of the 28th, Chief Prosecutor Zhou, accompanied by Prosecutor Du, court clerks, forensic doctors, inspectors, and police officers, went to conduct the autopsy. The autopsy revealed a wound on the right side of the deceased's skull, confirming that he died from the injury. Chief Prosecutor Zhou confirmed the findings and ordered the family to re-coffin the body. Wu Chungen was taken into custody, and Jiang Yisheng was released on bail pending further investigation.

Another Robbery in the City: A Mr. Wang from Nanmen was previously robbed of silver on the road, and the case remains unsolved. On the evening of the 26th, bandits approached the Xinyuanxing Silver Shop on Dongda Street in the city, requesting to buy a gold bracelet. The shop assistant declined, stating that the shop was closed. The bandits insisted that they needed to go to Shanghai the next morning. The assistant reluctantly took out several gold bracelets for them to see, at which point they snatched one and fled. The assistant and others were shocked and gave chase, but the bandits disappeared. They reported the incident to the Public Security Bureau and requested an investigation.

Gaoyou 110

Water Police Inspector Killed: The Finance Section of the county government dispatched staff member Jia Huachun to the 10th district to investigate tooth taxes. Upon arriving in Linze Town, Jia requested assistance from Yang Renzhi, the water police inspector stationed there, and ordered him to investigate the northern villages. While passing through Zhoujin River, Yang went to a teahouse for tea. Shortly after sitting down, six bandits arrived, each armed with guns. They grabbed Yang, shouting, "Are you Yang Renzhi?" After saying this, they took Yang away, tied him to a windmill in the field, and shot him in each of his limbs. Finally, they used a bayonet to cut out his heart. The bandits then fled.

Anhui Bandits Disturb Gaoyou: Jin Gou Town and Ta Er Ji, west of the lake in this county, are adjacent to Tianchang County in Anhui Province. Recently, a group of Anhui bandits has infiltrated the town, causing disturbances. County Chief Li has ordered the police team stationed west of the lake to suppress them.

Hangzhou 111

Hangzhou Mint Ordered to Close: The Hangzhou Mint has been closed for a long time due to a lack of silver. Factory Director Zhou Peizhen submitted a report to the Ministry of Finance requesting instructions on how to proceed. On the 27th, the Ministry of Finance sent a telegram ordering the factory to close immediately, appoint personnel to oversee its closure given the lack of silver for minting, and give employees two months' salary before dismissing them. The factory director was ordered to create a detailed inventory of all existing factory buildings, machinery, materials, documents, and accounts and submit it to the ministry for review, with the custodial personnel to be selected by the factory director. Director Zhou, upon receiving the order, has begun the closure process.

Swire's Yangtze River Steamer Wanliu Sinks After Hitting Reef 114

Losses Reach 600,000 Yuan

Only the Smokestack Remains Visible Above Water

Passengers and Crew Rescued

Commercial ship accidents have been frequent lately, with collisions and fires occurring one after another. After the Swire Company's Shengjing steamer was rescued from danger in Weihaiwei, the Wanliu steamer on the upper Yangtze River sank after hitting a reef. A reporter has investigated various sources and compiled the following report.

Cause of the Accident: Swire Company's Yangtze River upstream steamers are divided into large ships and shallow-draft vessels. There are three large ships: Wanxian, Wanliu, and Wantong. Each of these ships has a capacity of over 1,100 tons and operates annually after the Yangtze River floods. This year, all three ships were operating on the Sichuan River, traveling between Yichang and Chongqing. On this occasion, the Wanliu was transporting passengers and cargo from Chongqing to Wanxian and Yichang before heading to Shanghai. The river water was high. As the ship passed through the Huangjiapo river surface, approximately 140 to 150 miles from Chongqing, it strayed from the channel and entered a cluster of submerged reefs. The ship suddenly struck a reef, with its bow hitting the reef first, immediately causing a rupture.

Engine Damage: When the Wanliu struck the reef, the front of the ship was impaled. The bottom of the front hold was severely scraped by the reef, causing it to rupture. The middle hold, which housed the engine room, was the main part of the ship. When it was breached by the reef, river water rushed into the ship. Within moments, the water level in the front hold rose to eight feet. The engine room was also flooded within an hour, with the water reaching nine feet. The furnace in the engine room was extinguished by the water, plunging the ship into darkness and rendering it immobile. Fortunately, the hull was supported by the reef; otherwise, it would have sunk immediately.

Rescue of Crew and Passengers: When the ship struck the reef, the passengers were panicked and mindful of the Qijiang and Yiling ships sinking in the Yangduxi incident. Fearing the ship would sink in a minute, they rushed to the deck to escape. Fortunately, the captain and others reassured them that the ship was grounded on the reef and would not sink immediately. The passengers calmed down. The captain sent out distress signals and fired flares. Soon, many privately-owned wooden boats passed by and responded to the calls for help. The passengers were first transported to the private boats via sampans and gradually transported to Yichang. Subsequently, Swire in Chongqing received the telegram about the Wanliu accident and sent the Wanxian and other ships to help. Therefore, all crew and passengers were unharmed and safely arrived in Yichang.

Sinking of the Vessel: After the ship ran aground, the hull was severely damaged, and it gradually sank because of the heavy load. Luckily, the reef supported the vessel, so the sinking was somewhat slowed. Although the ship remains on the reef, the first two, three, and four holds are completely flooded. Currently, the water has submerged the third deck, leaving only the smokestack and ventilators visible above the water. The company is unable to salvage the ship now, as it must wait for the water level to drop in winter before attempting salvage operations.

Estimated Losses: The ship was one of Swire's first-class upper Yangtze River vessels, with a capacity of 1,180 tons. It was purchased from Longmao Foreign Firm in Shanghai as the Longmao wheel, and renamed the current name. The hull was built in the Jiangnan Shipyard, and the engine components were of excellent quality. The ship cost 400,000 yuan at the time of construction. In addition, the ship was carrying a large amount of cargo, including medicinal herbs and silk, which was all trapped in the ship. The loss of the cargo, as well as the luggage and money of the crew and passengers, is estimated to be at least 600,000 yuan. The company is planning to salvage the cargo from the holds that can be unloaded.

Disappearance of Russian 115

Confirmed Dead in Detention Center Due to Illness

Offer to Open Coffin for Examination

The case of the disappearance of Russian Gletzki from the Second Special District Court Prison has been heavily publicized by local Western newspapers, with some suggesting that it is a second Tafeng case. To clarify the truth, a reporter from this newspaper visited Ying Shi, the president of the Second Special District Court, yesterday. The reporter learned that the Western newspaper's report was untrue. According to the Second Special District Court Detention Center, a Russian named George Latakiaev died in the detention center on the 19th of this month at 11:40 AM due to illness. The Russian mentioned in the Western newspaper, Gletzki, does not exist. It is assumed that he is a misspelling of Latakiaev. The Russian had no home or job in Shanghai and begged for food on the streets. On the afternoon of the 16th of this month at 7:30 PM, he was found drunk and lying on vacant land near Bushi Road by the French Concession Deputy Constable Victoria. Victoria took him to the police station. The next day, the police department sent him to the Second Special District Court, accusing him of violating Article 25 of the Road Administration Regulations. The court sentenced him to two days of detention for drunkenness and five days of detention for extortion, for a total of seven days of detention. He was sent to the detention center, where he was already vomiting, appearing to have cholera. He was also gaunt and frail. After being detained in the detention center, he continued to vomit. The detention center's forensic doctor prescribed him medicines such as Ten Drops Water and Pingan Water, but they were ineffective. On the morning of the 19th at 11:40 AM, he died of illness. Prosecutor Wu Xiaoke and forensic doctor Wei Ligong conducted an autopsy and turned the body over to the Tongren Fuyuantang funeral home for burial. All of this is documented. The court denied the claim that the Russian was beaten to death by prison guards in the detention center. They declared that if foreigners still had suspicions, they could open the coffin for examination to see if there were any injuries, so that the truth of the case could be revealed. A letter from the Jiangsu-Shanghai Second Special District Prison stated: "Dear Sir, we read in your paper on the 29th of this month a report from the Da Mei Evening News about the disappearance of Russian Gletzki in prison. We were shocked. After checking, this prison has not received any Russian prisoners under the name of Gletzki since its establishment. No foreign prisoners have died or disappeared. This is purely fabricated. We are deeply concerned that the rumors are false and request that your newspaper make a correction. Sincerely, Jiangsu-Shanghai Second Special District Prison, June 29th."

A letter from the Jiangsu-Shanghai Second Special District Court Clerk's Office stated: "Dear Sir, we read a news item in the Da Mei Evening News stating that a Russian newspaper staff member, Glacken, disappeared from the jail of the Second Special District Court in the French Concession. Some people saw him bleeding, and it is suspected that he was beaten in the chest. We were shocked. After checking, this court's detention center has not held any prisoners named Glacken. It is possible that it is a mistake for the Russian Georgi Latakiaev. The prisoner was found drunk on the ground on the evening of the 16th of this month, violating police regulations. The French Concession Police Department sent him to this court for trial on the 17th. The interrogation revealed that the prisoner was homeless and lived by begging. The charge of being drunk and lying on the ground was true. He was immediately sentenced to seven days of detention and sent to this court's detention center. The prisoner had already contracted a serious illness outside and was weak and emaciated when he entered the prison. He vomited and had diarrhea. The prison doctor examined him and determined that he had contracted an epidemic. He was given medicine, but it did not improve. Just as he was about to be transferred to a hospital for treatment, he died in the prison at 11:40 AM on the morning of the 19th. The office prepared a document and reported it to the prosecutor's office of this court. The prosecutor's office sent Prosecutor Wu Xiaoke and forensic doctor Wei Ligong to the prison for inspection. The inspection confirmed that he died of illness and there was no other reason. Shanghai Tongren Fuyuantang was ordered to provide coffins and bury him. There are files and certificates to prove this. The Jiangsu-Shanghai Second Special District Prison is directly under the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. After inquiries with the prison, it was found that there was no such incident. The above news is obviously fabricated out of thin air. In addition to sending a letter to the newspaper requesting a correction and investigation, we hope that you will check and make a correction. Sincerely, Jiangsu-Shanghai Second Special District Court Clerk's Office, June 29th."

Western Newspaper Reports on the Atrocities of the Japanese Army in Northeast China 116

German Priest Lai Pu Tragically Murdered: The Zi Lin Bao (North China Daily News) published details yesterday regarding the murder of German Priest Lai Pu near Longjing Village on the Manchu-Korean border. The details were obtained from reliable sources stating that after Priest Lai was taken away by Japanese soldiers, he never returned. His body was later found buried in the ground nearby, covered with wounds and with broken limbs. This incident shows the atrocities of the Japanese in Northeast China. On June 5th, a German priest died of typhus in Tai Ye Tang (transliteration). The archbishop sent a priest to the nearby Japanese police station to call the Japanese Consulate in Yanji, asking them to inform Priest Lai Pu in Longjing Village to take care of the matter. That afternoon, Priest Lai Pu took a light train to Laotougou. He arrived in the evening and met several priests and parishioners from Yanji who also wanted to go to Tai Ye Tang. Because it was late and raining, they decided to stay overnight and leave the next day. However, Priest Lai Pu was eager to attend the funeral, so he ignored the advice and took a horse sent by Tai Ye Tang to pick him up, braving the rain. When he arrived in Enhasi (transliteration), it was already 9:00 PM. There was a Japanese garrison there. The Korean translator sent by Tai Ye Tang was standing next to the Japanese sentry, waiting. As soon as Lai arrived, the Japanese sentry said to the Korean translator, "What kind of pig is this? Tell him to dismount immediately." Lai replied that he was completely soaked and wanted to go to Tai Ye Tang, and handed him his business card. The sentry shouted, "Do you know that no one dares to hand a business card to a Japanese soldier while on horseback?" Then the two sentries began to scold him. The other soldiers in the garrison came out after hearing the noise, and they were all drunk. Then a Japanese military policeman came and shouted, "What's going on?" When he saw Priest Lai Pu, he said, "Get off your horse!" Lai obeyed and dismounted. The Japanese military policeman immediately slapped him in the face. The other Japanese soldiers surrounded Lai, dispersed the crowd, and severely beat the Korean translator until he was covered in blood. They then took Lai to the garrison. The Korean translator could only faintly hear the sounds of beatings outside, and then heard a scream. He ran back to Tai Ye Tang and reported to the archbishop that the Japanese were going to kill Priest Lai Pu. The archbishop immediately took two priests to rescue him. They rushed to the riverbank and heard three gunshots, followed by a fourth. They suspected that they were being shot at and had to turn back. A Korean in Enhasi (transliteration) heard the sound of horses' hooves and people's voices, and looked out the door. He saw a man leading a horse, with three Japanese soldiers on the side and three Japanese soldiers behind. The Korean asked, "Are you Priest Lai Pu?" The man leading the horse replied, "Yes, I am Lai Pu." Before he finished speaking, a Japanese soldier rushed towards the Korean, who dodged into the room. A few minutes later, he heard three gunshots, followed by another. The Korean changed into black clothes and went out, and saw the Japanese soldiers returning alone. He did not see Priest Lai Pu. Knowing that something was wrong, he secretly went to the riverbank with a friend to search. They found Lai Pu's body lying face down in a pool of blood. They took off his outer clothing and took it to the Tai Ye Tang Church to report. The church servant told him not to disturb the archbishop for the time being. He was only able to see the archbishop at 4:00 AM and tell him what had happened. The archbishop immediately sent a priest with him to Enhasi. They first went to the pool of blood and saw that Lai Pu's body was no longer there, but there was still blood. They found four bullets. The priest then went alone to the Japanese garrison in Enhasi and saw the Korean translator hired by the Japanese army. He asked if he had seen Priest Lai Pu. The translator replied that he had. The priest asked where he was. The translator said, "He is here. The Japanese soldiers beat him, but the injuries were not fatal. I told the Japanese soldiers that he was a priest and should be released immediately." The priest asked if he had been released. The translator said yes. The priest asked where he was. The translator said that he had gone to Hengsheng Laizi (transliteration). The priest said, "That's strange. Why did he go there?" The translator said, "That road is very dangerous, and something might happen to him." The priest then returned. Later, he saw a horse abandoned in the wilderness, with wounds on its body. Two days later, a Korean saw footprints in the sand and followed them. He found Priest Lai Pu's body buried in shallow soil. He examined the body and saw that there were stab wounds and club wounds on the skull, the nose was broken, the flesh of the nose was cut into three pieces, there was a bullet wound in the heart, and a bullet wound in the abdomen, both of which had passed through. One arm was almost dislocated, and one arm was broken. There were a total of thirty-five stab wounds on the chest, abdomen, back, and thighs. It was truly tragic.

A Record of the Sanmen Bay Inspection (1) 117

Departure from Shanghai and Inspection Along the Way

The History of the Dongmen Island Lighthouse

Sanmen Bay in eastern Zhejiang is one of China's famous good harbors. In 1929, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce sought permission from the central government to open a self-governed commercial port. The central government and the Zhejiang provincial government commissioned a committee to survey and determine the areas for administration, commerce, agriculture, salt production, and residential areas throughout the bay. A preliminary plan was prepared. Overseas Chinese in various places felt a great interest in the construction of Sanmen Bay. They organized the Sanmen Bay Overseas Chinese Construction Committee to actively engage in construction, cooperating with the government using the power of the masses. On September 24th of last year, the committee gathered representatives from all walks of life and went to Sanmen Bay for the first on-site inspection. On June 24th, the committee's representatives launched a second inspection, departing from Shanghai, passing through Dinghai and Shipu, and arriving at Sanmen Bay. They returned to Shanghai on the 29th. This newspaper reporter also participated in this mission and will record the findings below. It is hoped that patriots in the country will hear about it and raise funds together so that the mission of the first major port in the East can be achieved soon.

Organization of the Inspection Group: The Sanmen Bay Overseas Chinese Construction Committee was the main body of the inspection group. It also hired American engineer Warner, a road construction engineer from Kai Dui Pi La, and Liu Zhongchang, a mechanical and electrical engineer from Lihe Foreign Firm, to inspect road and dam construction projects throughout the bay. The inspection group consisted of eleven people, including representatives from the Sanmen Bay Overseas Chinese Construction Committee: Zhou Nai Weng, Hu Changying, Zhou Liuting, Chen Xinyuan, Li Jingru; Yu Lianpin, director of the Hangzhou Radio Station; Yang Zhuoqun, representative of Tongyixiang Silk Factory; Wu Weimin, representative of Huayuan Tongsheng Silk Weaving Factory; American engineer Warner; Chinese engineer Liu Zhongchang; and this newspaper reporter Qian Hua. It was reported that more than ten representatives from the Zhejiang Provincial Government and various sectors were also planning to attend, but due to the urgency of time, they were unable to do so. Wang Wenhan, director of the Zhejiang Outer Sea Water Police Bureau, sent a Tai'an warship, which waited in Shipu, to transport the inspection group to Sanmen Bay for their safety.

Shanghai to Sanmen Bay: From Shanghai to Sanmen Bay, it takes 18 hours by boat. The six boats that dock at the 16th Pier every week, including the Zhoushan, Chuanshan, Dahua, Daxing, Taizhou, and Deli, can all pass through Dinghai and arrive at Shipu, the entrance to Sanmen Bay. Then, passengers change to Yongpu and Linpu launches to inspect the port area of Haiyou Port in Sanmen Bay. The inspection group departed from the 16th Pier on the Daxing boat at 5:00 PM on the 24th of this month and arrived at Dinghai at 4:00 AM the next morning. Dinghai, commonly known as Zhoushan, is the largest island in eastern Zhejiang. It is surrounded by the sea and not connected to the mainland. Most of the residents are engaged in fishing and salt production, and the market is thriving. The scenery is particularly beautiful, with green mountains and blue waters, like a painting. Nearby small islands are scattered like stars, surrounded by mountains, forming a natural barrier. It is said that Zhoushan has sixteen layers of gates, which shows the excellence of its terrain. The whole group went ashore to sightsee, walking hundreds of steps to climb the Dongyue Temple on the top of Dongyue Mountain, overlooking the entire city. They then returned to the city, circled around it, and returned to the boat. At 7:00 AM, the Daxing boat left the port and headed south to Shipu Town, the entrance to Sanmen Bay. The boat traveled between the islands and mountains, winding and turning. Looking out from the boat, one felt like an immortal. According to navigators, the inland sea route from Dinghai is dangerous, with reefs everywhere and rapid currents. The slightest carelessness can lead to collisions and capsizing. At 10:30 AM, the boat reached Tongwamen, the gateway to Shipu. Looking from afar, the mountains connect to form a straight line. At first glance, it seems that the waterway is blocked and impassable. But as the boat approached the foot of the mountain, a line of waterway was revealed, which was truly a natural barrier. After entering Tongwamen, Shipu Pier was reached in half an hour. Although Shipu is a small town, it is a necessary stop for navigation in eastern Zhejiang. Therefore, the market is bustling, and the residents are prosperous. It has electric lights and radio equipment. The houses on the hillside are densely arranged. Climbing the steps, one has a different view. At this time, the Taian warship was anchored in the river. Captain Sun Xianhe came to greet them. At 10:00 PM on the 25th, the whole group boarded the ship to rest. At 2:00 AM on the 26th, they weighed anchor and set sail for Sanmen Bay.

The Lighthouse on Dongmen Island: Reefs are common in the inland seas of eastern Zhejiang, which navigators consider a dangerous route. The region lacks lighthouses at crucial places, which has resulted in frequent shipwrecks. Brothers Ren Xiaohe and Ren Xiaofu from Shipu, who have personal experience of this issue, demolished their home in 1914 to build a lighthouse on Dongmen Island near Shipu. They used their monthly income from fishing to cover the lighthouse's operational expenses and their remaining funds for construction and expansion. In recent years, the lighthouse's architecture has been completely renovated, costing more than 10,000 yuan. They built seven residential buildings next to the tower, where the brothers live year-round. Since the establishment of the lighthouse, ships have been able to pass through safely without incident.

The Tai'an Cruiser on Which the Inspection Group Traveled 118

The Scenery of Haiyou Port in Sanmen Bay 119

Dongmen Island Lighthouse 120

Page 10

The villagers admired his righteousness, so they erected a monument next to the tower. He always said that running the lighthouse was difficult. After the inspection team arrived in Shipu, they hired a small boat at 3 pm that afternoon to visit the Dongmen Island Lighthouse. Mr. Ren Xiaofu warmly greeted them. Mr. Ren, with a benevolent face, said that he was already fifty-four years old, and his brother was fifty-seven. He had studied in a private school for three years. Building the lighthouse was for the benefit of others in the fishing industry. He and his brother had been fishermen since they were young and were not from a wealthy family. All that they had earned from decades of hard work was invested in this. They currently had two large fishing boats, and the monthly profit of over one hundred yuan was just enough to cover the expenses of the lighthouse. However, his brothers were getting old and weak, and after their death, the lighthouse would eventually have no means of support. Therefore, they were trying to figure out how to purchase farmland as a permanent fund. He did not know when this wish could be fulfilled, and he was always worried about it. His spirit of sacrificing for public good was enough to shame the officials of today. The residence next to the tower, although extremely simple, was elegantly arranged, with flowers and trees filling the garden, and fragrance overflowing. The sea breeze blew, making one feel refreshed, almost as if one were on a fairy island. It was said that a local gentleman had petitioned the Ministry of Finance on behalf of the Ren family, requesting subsidies. In the nineteenth year of the Republic of China (1930), the Zhejiang Customs had allocated a one-time subsidy of one thousand five hundred yuan, but thereafter, it was stopped due to the national financial difficulties. Although it rained heavily that day, the interest of the visitors was increased by Mr. Ren’s righteousness. The monument next to the tower was inscribed by the famous Huangyan calligrapher Yu Changlin. The inscription read: "Dongmen Island stands tall in the sea, serving as a shield for Xiangshan Shipu. It is the Tianmen Mountain mentioned in old gazetteers. The Changguo Guard City was established here in the Tang Dynasty. The islands are scattered, with the Tongwamen port to the north and the Laodongmen port to the south. It is an important passage for the Sanmen Bay route. Whenever there is fog at night, the harbor entrance is indistinguishable, and ships passing by are in danger, making it a dreaded route. In the spring of the year Yimao (1915), the islanders Ren Xiaohe and Xiaofu brothers raised money to build a lighthouse on the southeast of the island to guide the route, thus celebrating peace. In the autumn of the year Jiwei (1919), due to carelessness, the tower was destroyed. The Xiaohe brothers, together with Ji Junzhuan, Chang Deng, and others, raised funds to expand the three-story lighthouse and build seven houses next to the tower as a place for the lamp operator to live. The kitchen was fully equipped, and the construction was solid and durable, costing over ten thousand yuan in total, sacrificing their homes to do good deeds. From then on, the sea waves no longer caused fear, and merchants sang praises. The benevolent and righteous spirit of the Ren brothers is immortal along with this tower, without end for billions of years. Changlin is also from Zhejiang, sharing in the celebration, so he wrote this record to inform those who come later and pass it on to future generations. Written by Yu Lin of Huangyan in the first month of autumn in the year Jiazi (1924)."

Li Shijia Crossed to Japan Yesterday Morning 125

Negotiating the Ninghai New Warship Matter

Japanese Technician Jinbo Accompanied

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Strives to Stop Jiangsu Special Business Tax 126

If the Central Government Cannot Sanction Illegal Acts

It Has Already Abandoned Its Clear Decree to Abolish Li Taxes

Since hearing the news that the Jiangsu Provincial Government planned to implement a special business consumption tax, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, based on the request of various industry guilds, has repeatedly submitted to the Executive Yuan, requesting its cancellation in order to uphold the law. However, although the Executive Yuan has issued an order to cancel it, the Jiangsu Provincial Government still intends to illegally collect it from July 1st. The Chamber of Commerce yesterday again submitted letters from the seven industries and telegraphed the Executive Yuan to effectively stop it. The telegram is recorded below:

(Title omitted) It is noted that the source of tax revenue to offset the abolition of Li taxes belongs to the Central Government as consolidated tax and to the local government as business tax. The boundaries have long been determined. The Jiangsu Province’s Li tax was assigned to the Central Government as early as after Minister Song took over the Ministry of Finance, and the Ding and Cao taxes, which had always been national taxes, were allocated back to Jiangsu Province. The gains and losses were sufficient to offset each other, so the abolition of the Li tax can be said to have caused no significant loss in Jiangsu Province. The actual amount of loss to the Provincial Government is only the surtax of 20% added to the account (which continues to be collected and retained for provincial use even after the account is closed). In terms of numbers, it is definitely not too large. If the business tax is managed properly, it should not be insufficient to offset it. The Province’s tax revenue deficit is partly due to the excessive collection costs at the beginning of the business tax and partly due to the impact of the situation, which has prevented business from improving, resulting in sluggish tax revenue. The situation is just like the reduction or exemption of Ding and Cao taxes due to poor harvest, which is the same in principle. When the state encounters a year of poor harvest of fields, it can only reduce or exempt taxes according to precedent, and there is no other way to extract from farmers. In the same way, there is no reason to change the name and take compensation from merchants due to the poor collection of business tax. This is on the political system. Furthermore, the business tax law was decided by the Legislative Yuan and promulgated by the National Government. The tax laws and collection methods are all stipulated. The Province, knowing that it has no basis, does not hesitate to create a special business tax name to confront it. This measure has long exceeded the scope of the law. If the Jiangsu Provincial Government, which is close to the capital, does not hesitate to disregard the clear decree to abolish the Li tax, how can the central government's decrees be implemented nationwide in the future? The shortage of treasury funds is not unique to Jiangsu Province. Other provinces may have ten or hundreds of times more. Abandoning the political system and disregarding the law due to lack of funds means there is no day for political integrity. This is why Confucianism talks about politics; they say that one should rather give up food than give up faith. Recently, business sentiment in Jiangsu Province has been agitated to the extreme, and they say that if the Central Government cannot sanction the illegal acts of Jiangsu Province, the Central Government has already abandoned its clear decree to abolish the Li tax. The so-called offsetting the abolition of the Li tax has lost its basis for existence. There is only the suspension of the consolidated tax and business tax. I am afraid that a great disturbance will be unstoppable once it starts, adding to the government's anxieties. Therefore, I do not avoid being troubles煩 and offer my sincere opinion. I respectfully request the President to effectively stop the special business tax in Jiangsu Province for the sake of public convenience. Shanghais Municipal Chamber of Commerce respectfully bows in investigation.

Record of the General Assembly of the Silk Factory Trade Association 128

Unable to Operate Due to Increased Burdens. The Shanghai Silk Factory Trade Association held its 13th Temporary Representative Assembly of the First Session at 3 p.m. yesterday (29th). More than 70 people, including representatives of various silk factories and standing committee members Zhu Jingan and Zhang Peishen, were present. The meeting was held as usual. First, Chairman Shen Chen reported on the association's work process and cases: (1) Since the last meeting, the association has handled a total of 186 documents. (2) Changes in the number of representatives of the association attending the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce. (3) Payment of the municipal chamber of commerce membership fees. (4) The Industrial Department organized and reorganized the Jiangsu-Zhejiang陳 Factory Silk and陳繭 Committee. (5) Shanghai Hengtaixiang Exchange Bank went bankrupt. If any industry has匯兌 款 owed by the bank, they must find a guarantor to collect the款 from the association before July 15. If any industry is involved, please pay attention. After the report, three important cases were discussed: (1) A discussion on the strike that occurred in various silk factories in the Hongkou District due to wage issues. The consensus was that this strike and the demands for improved treatment were not the true intentions of the labor union, but were caused by incitement from a third party. The truth is not only understood by the industry, but also by the party and government agencies and labor unions. However, the silk industry is related to industry and commerce and should take into account all three aspects. Judging from the current cost, this year's new繭 from Zhejiang Province has the highest cost, requiring 530 taels per dan of silk, and at least 400 taels. Jiangsu Province requires a maximum of 450 taels and a minimum of 390 taels. Adding in the silk reeling and female worker wages of 42 cents per work, the cost of each dan of silk is about 550 taels to 650 taels. According to the current market, the price of foreign silk is only over 500 taels, and the factory is still losing more than 100 taels, and there is no real transaction. It is investigated that most of the factories currently in operation are reeling陳繭 for押欵 (the cost of陳繭 is over 1,000 taels, and the loss is even greater). Only a few are reeling new繭, purely to maintain the livelihoods of the workers, and there is no profit to be made. If they want to continue to support it, the factories are already finding it difficult. However, according to this year's繭 price, farmers and sericulturists will also go bankrupt. If we abandon the difficulties of farmers and merchants and only seek to increase wages, then the international trade of raw silk will only lead to its extinction. The consensus of the industry is that it is already a great fortune if they can maintain the status quo and work hard. If they increase the burden again, the industry will be unable to continue operating. Then, Zhang Peishen, the director of the Hongkou District Silk Factory Association, stood up and reported that since the strike occurred in the Hongkou District Silk Factory, the workers of each factory had met several times. They were very shocked that the request to restore the original treatment was being published in the name of others. The workers knew the factory's difficulties very well. The factories currently in operation are for the sake of maintaining the workers' livelihoods and were started after the workers and management reached an understanding in advance. This labor unrest was clearly caused by others stirring up trouble, and the workers had no demands at all. The workers of each silk factory have elected representatives, including Xiang Cheng, Shen Shaoqin, Yi Chang, Tan Yongyuan, Cheng Wangziqing, Tong Wei, Ye Qiutao, Yu Jing, Ding Guanfang, Yi Feng, Wei Kun, Wang Yuanfeng, Ren Ji, Yin Jianqing, Xing Lun, Xu Chunqiao, Wei Yu, Cha Wenqiao, and Song Ziqiao, to sign a statement of fact and declare that the wage cannot be increased any further to maintain the status quo. (2) A discussion on the issue of the association's collection of this year's membership fees. Chairman Shen said that the association has always collected the Fuyin business fee for each district, which is one yuan per car, and the association's membership fee is 50 cents. Now, there are few factories in operation, and the revenue is not enough to handle welfare matters, so they have temporarily suspended collection. The association's membership fee is related to regular expenses and is planned to be collected in two installments, totaling 50 cents, to cover office expenses. It was resolved to do so. (3) A discussion on the letter from the Shanghai National Crisis Savings Association Preparatory Office, reporting on the progress of the preparations and requesting the election of representatives. It was resolved to wait until the next public recommendation. After the discussion, just as the meeting was about to adjourn, two female worker representatives came to the meeting and reported to Chairman Shen that several factories in the Zhabei District had been affected by labor unrest. Chairman Shen comforted the two representatives and promised to investigate and verify. By the time the meeting adjourned, it was already 7 p.m.

A Dead Body Lying on the Bed in a Small House 132

Hands and Feet Were Bound, Neck and Nose Were Injured

The Circumstances Indicate That the Body Was Moved After Death

No. 396 Laoshifu Road, French Concession is a new small house built not long ago. At around 2 p.m. yesterday, a cleaner, Mr. Jia, who was in charge of managing the houses in the area, was sweeping and came to the entrance of that number. He suddenly caught a glimpse of the light in the house that had not been turned off, and he was very suspicious. He stood at the door and shouted loudly for a long time, but no one answered. Seeing that the gate and fence were not closed, he pushed open the fence and entered. There was still no one there. He looked around the living room for a week. There was a reception table in the center, but nothing else. Several pairs of couplets were hung on the walls. One of them was signed "Ke Kun" at the top and "Dongshan樵子 Xie Hua" at the bottom, and "Xie Chen" at the top and "Xu Shiying" at the bottom. He climbed the stairs. There was only a half-iron bed in the front building, and the rest was scattered debris piled on the ground. When he looked at the back building, he suddenly saw a male corpse lying on the iron bed. At this point, Mr. Jia ran downstairs in extreme shock and immediately alerted the neighbors. They all gathered together and immediately reported it to the police. The police immediately sent detectives to investigate. They found that the deceased was about 30 years old, wearing a Western-style suit on the upper body and Chinese trousers on the lower body. His hands and feet were tightly bound, and there was a very deep knife wound on his neck and nose. There was an old mat on the floor, with bright red bloodstains on it. The situation indicated that he had probably been bound on the mat first, then stabbed to death, and then moved to the bed. The detectives then carried the corpse by car to the autopsy center of Tongrenfuyuan for an autopsy and reported to the Second Special Court for examination.

Courtroom Spectacle: Lu Lan Chun 133

Lu's Testimony Loud and Clear

Yu Weiwen's Lawsuit Rejected

The actress Lu Lan Chun, who once enjoyed great fame, suddenly had a man from Yancheng named Yu Weiwen (also known as Yu Cai Zhi), claiming to be Lu's father, involved in a lawsuit with her. This went to the third instance court, where Yu ultimately lost, and the matter was put to rest. Unexpectedly, at the end of last year, Yu suddenly sued Lu for abandonment in the First Special District District Court. Because Lu had married Xue Gengsheng, he referred to her as Xue Yu Shi. The court, based on the indictment, considered it a case involving direct relatives, which does not fall under the provisions for self-representation (private prosecution). Therefore, without holding a hearing, it ruled to reject the private prosecution. Yu was still dissatisfied and appealed to the Second Branch of the High Court, which was also rejected. Now, Yu has hired lawyer Song Yunhui, changed Cai Zhi to Weiwen, and filed another private prosecution with the First Special Court. He refers to the defendant not as Xue Yu Shi, but by her stage name. The cause of action, however, remains abandonment. The trial was originally scheduled for the afternoon of the day before yesterday, but at that time, the presiding judge, Mr. Wu Tingqi, was occupied with another case and could not attend to this one. It was postponed to yesterday afternoon. After 2:00 PM, many people arrived to observe. The original plaintiff and defendant, as well as their respective lawyers, also arrived at the Second Tribunal one after another. Lu Lan Chun, now thirty-six years old, still retains her charm. Her long hair has been cut short, with a fringe covering her forehead. She wears a simple dark-colored, small checkered woolen qipao (cheongsam) and embroidered white satin boots. She speaks with a Beijing accent. Because she is accustomed to acting as a male lead, her voice is loud and clear, easily heard by everyone in the courtroom. Her demeanor is also very poised and generous. At 3:30 PM, Judge Wu finished hearing the other case and turned to this one. He first asked the names, ages, and addresses of both parties, then instructed the plaintiff, "You already filed a private prosecution against the defendant in December of last year, which this court ruled to reject according to the law. The ruling was delivered to your proxy lawyer, Zheng Wenkai, on January 13th of this year. You were still dissatisfied and filed an appeal, but the result was also a rejection. Why are you filing a private prosecution again now?" Yu, upon hearing this instruction, claimed ignorance of the previous ruling. After the judge tossed the ruling for his review, he simply repeated his grievances. He then began to describe the past conflicts with the defendant, which did not seem relevant to the present case. The judge stopped him. Lu's defense lawyers, Wu Linkun and Wang [missing character], immediately requested that the plaintiff's suit be rejected again. They stated that this private prosecution by the plaintiff, except for the change of name, is based on the same facts as the previous suit. The law stipulates that a case that has already been prosecuted cannot be brought before the same court again. Therefore, this case should be dismissed. This kind of lawsuit may not be the intent of the private prosecutor himself. For example, in the previous indictment, they referred to themselves as father and daughter, but now they say adopted daughter. All of this is likely a scheme devised by his lawyer to try to deceive the court. The judicial authorities have long had instructions regarding lawyers handling cases. This kind of behavior not only violates the law but also greatly harms lawyer's ethics, and so on. The plaintiff's lawyer declared that they were proceeding according to the client's instructions. Judge Wu then ruled to dismiss the private prosecution. After the ruling, the crowd of observers dispersed like a tide.

Xue's Nephew's Inheritance Dispute Appealed: Ruling 134

Original Ruling Upheld, Nephew Wins

Appeal and Cross-Appeal Rejected

Hua Li Hou is the son-in-law of the late wealthy merchant Xue [missing character]run. Last year, after Xue's death, his estate was divided among his sons. Hua, based on current laws, believed that his deceased wife was also entitled to a share, and although his wife was deceased, her children should inherit in her place. Therefore, in the name of his son, Hua Shuanggu, and daughter, Hua Manyun, as their legal guardian, he hired lawyers Yang Linzhi, Ye Shaoying, Zhang Jiahui, etc., to file a lawsuit against his brothers-in-law, Xue Jiasheng, Yansheng, and Gengsheng, to divide the property. The First Special District District Court ruled that the defendants should jointly pay the plaintiffs two-thirds of 500,000 yuan. The Xues, dissatisfied with the ruling, listed their reasons and filed an appeal, which was also concluded after review by the Second Branch of the High Court, which announced that it would set a date for judgment, as detailed in this newspaper. At that time, Hua Li Hou's side, because they had requested 500,000 yuan but were only awarded two-thirds, and also because the Xue side appealed, also filed a cross-appeal, stating that his son, Hua Yi Hong, had renounced his inheritance rights, which was an internal matter among the heirs. The original ruling only granted two-thirds because he was not included in the lawsuit, which was illegal. Furthermore, because the Xues were suspected of selling, transferring, and squandering the estate, they specifically requested a declaration of provisional execution. Now, the Civil Division Chief of the court, Hu Yigu, and judges Ye and Cai, have announced the judgment: "Main text: The appeal and cross-appeal are both rejected. The costs of the second instance litigation shall be borne by each party." The reasoning for the judgment, regarding the appeal portion, is divided into two points: (1) Regarding the issue of inheritance by representation, Article 1140 of the Civil Code states that if a first-priority heir as specified in Article 1138 dies or loses their inheritance rights before the commencement of inheritance, their direct lineal descendants shall inherit their share by representation. Furthermore, Article 2 of the Enforcement Act of the Inheritance Section of the Civil Code states that even if the commencement of inheritance occurred before the implementation of the Inheritance Section of the Civil Code, but after the following dates, women also have inheritance rights to the estates of their direct lineal ascendants: (1) The date of the second National Congress of the Chinese Kuomintang's resolution on the women's movement reaching each province after being communicated by the Judicial Administration Committee in October of the 15th year of the Republic of China; (2) The date of the communication to provinces not yet under the jurisdiction of the National Government, or the date they came under jurisdiction, etc. In this case, the deceased, Xue Baorun, passed away in this city in August of the 19th year of the Republic of China. The commencement of inheritance was after being under the jurisdiction of the National Government. Although the respondents' mother died before the commencement of inheritance, according to the special provisions above, the respondents are entitled to claim inheritance by representation according to the Inheritance Law, regardless of when the death of the inheritor occurred. The interpretations of the Judicial Yuan Nos. 405 and 424 have lost their effect due to the implementation of the Inheritance Section of the Civil Code, and the appellants cannot invoke them to argue that the respondents have no right to inherit by representation. (2) Regarding the issue of estate division, the appellants claim that the estate has already been divided. The evidence they presented is the will of the appellants' father and the certificate of managing the estate. Although the will states that the property is to be managed and distributed by the four appellants, it is insufficient to prove whether it has already been divided. Furthermore, at the time the will was written, the law had already clearly recognized women's right to inherit property, but the will designated all property to be inherited by the four appellants, disregarding other heirs. This violates the mandatory legal regulations, and this will does not have legal effect. The certificate of managing the estate is a small part of the estate. A detailed translation of the certificate's wording indicates that it is to be jointly managed by the appellants and cannot be designated as evidence that it has already been divided. Furthermore, the appellants have not presented any evidence that it has been definitively divided. Therefore, they cannot claim that it has already been divided to counter the respondents' request for analysis, etc. The reasoning for the cross-appeal portion is also divided into two points: (1) Regarding the issue of inheritance share; (2) Regarding the issue of provisional execution. However, they are not very important news, so they are omitted.

Detective Liu investigated for several days and confirmed the existence of this fake organization. At 9:15 AM the day before yesterday, together with Chinese Detective Chief You Agen, he went to the address and arrested Mao Shunfu from Shanghai, Wang Kedong from Hangzhou, Wu He from Wuxi, Lu Jinquan from Tongzhou, Jin Dongsheng from Baoshan, Xu Ciyuan from Shanghai, and six others. Six seals of the New Army 37th Army, eighty-five symbols, two commission certificates, eighty envelopes, one instruction book, and a large number of military documents were confiscated and brought to the police station. It was found that Xu Yuanyuan was the main culprit in the case and the "Division Commander" of the "Second Division" of the "Thirty-Seventh Army." Later, at room 13 of the Dong'an Hotel at 245 Guangdong Road, Zhou Guangzu from Changzhou, Jiang Zhonglin from Wuxi, Liu Zefang from Changzhou, Tang Ating, Zheng Bingzhang, Yang Binggang, Xu Guansheng, and Ding Mingyuan were arrested. Including the previous arrests, a total of fourteen people were detained separately. The police station sent them to the First Special Court's Criminal Division 1 yesterday morning. Mao Afu and Xu Ciyuan both hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend them, and Tang Ating hired lawyer Jiang Chiping to defend him. The police station's lawyer, Ru Baoyi, stated that the Municipal Public Security Bureau had sent personnel to the case requesting a transfer, with official documents, but the Public Security Bureau only knew that the police station had arrested seven suspects, so the official documents only requested the transfer of seven suspects. Whether the case should be handled by the Public Security Bureau or the court, and whether the police station had not investigated clearly due to time constraints, was requested to be postponed to facilitate research on the issue of acceptance and to investigate who was related and who was not, so that they could separately request legal action or release. Interrogated Xu Ciyuan, confessed to being the Division Commander of the Second Division of the 37th Army, but claimed that he was commissioned by the Army Commander Chen Shenghao and that the army was stationed in Wuhan. But he did not know who commissioned Chen. The other defendants all claimed that they were visiting friends at the two hotels and were mistakenly arrested. Judge Qian Hongye reviewed the confessions and ordered the case to be adjourned and the defendants returned to detention separately.

Gu Baosen Hiding in Hotel

Plaintiff to Find a Way to Identify and Arrest

Tan Ying, a female actress from the Lianhua Film Company, recently, together with her mother Tan Wang Shi (from Nanjing, residing at 7 Runde Lane, Zhenzhu Street, Nanshi), hired lawyers Xu Qinpu and Zhang Chongding to file a private prosecution with the Criminal Division of the District Court against Gu Baosen (also known as Gu Xiaochun), an architect residing at 5 Yude Lane, Dong Tangjia Lane in this city, for seducing a young woman, requesting legal punishment and bringing a related civil suit. At this point, lawyer Zhang stated, "Please postpone the trial for one week so that the plaintiffs can make further efforts to investigate the defendant's hiding place and ensure that the defendant is arrested and brought to justice." Next, Tan Ying was asked if she had a relationship with the defendant, and she answered, "Yes." The judge then approved the postponement for review.

National Medicine Industry Labor Strike Heard Yesterday 138

Since the representatives of the workers and the representatives of the National Medicine Trade Association, Zhang Meian, negotiated and talked the day before yesterday, both parties held meetings yesterday, and it is feared that it will not be resolved in a short time.

(2) Investigate the names of non-members in various stores, negotiate with the Trade Association, and request that unemployed members be supplemented. The resolution was passed. It was decided to appoint Yi Guifang, Yu Guiqing, Shen Ziheng, Li Baokang, Xie Jixian, Zhong Debao, and Chen Weiming to be responsible for handling everything. The above cases were submitted to the Trade Union Council for approval and decision. The announcement was published, telling the employed members of the suffering of unemployment and asking for unified assistance.

Trade Association Emergency Meeting The National Medicine Trade Association held a second emergency executive committee meeting yesterday to discuss the three requests put forward by the Trade Union representatives. Chairman Cen Zhiliang decided that the requests made by the Trade Union were of great importance, and the entire executive committee should not handle them first. It will be submitted to the members' representative assembly on July 5 for discussion and processing. Regarding the facts of the negotiations between the Trade Union representatives and Zhang Meian, a standing committee member of the association, the association will issue a solemn statement to correct the public's perception and eliminate all misunderstandings.

Employer Statement The National Medicine Trade Association reported yesterday that the representatives of the Pharmacy Trade Union and Zhang Meian, a member of the Standing Committee of the association, had negotiated the results. Zhang stated that the original labor-capital contract proposed by the union continued to be valid, and the employer was not allowed to arbitrarily break it, as well as a salary increase of 10 yuan per person per month, and the placement of unemployed workers. The three requirements were fully accepted and promised to be submitted to the meeting for approval before a formal reply. The association considered the record to be untrue. The general employer was even more terrified after seeing the disclosure of this news, and they went to the meeting one after another to inquire about the truth. The association specially declared the actual situation of the negotiations a few days ago as follows: The Trade Union sent Zhao Fang, Feng Chen, Zhu and other five representatives to the association a few days ago, proposing that the employer should not break the labor-capital conditions, continue to hire substitutes, accept the placement of unemployed workers, and require a salary increase of 10 yuan. The four measures were requested to be fully answered by the association. The standing committee member of the association, Zhang Meian, answered item by item, saying that the employer has always abided by the conditions and has never broken them. However, the association may have difficulty in taking care of everything. If the union can report the facts of a store breaking the conditions, the association will severely correct it. If it is generally said that the employer has broken the conditions, it is very empty. It is up to the employer to hire substitutes, and the union must not force the union. If the union must force it, the employer will refuse the placement of unemployed workers according to law in order to protect its powers, and the association has already opposed the request for a salary increase of 10 yuan at the executive committee meeting. There is absolutely no room for discussion. However, if the union can take into account the social stability and does not want to expand the strike, the association expresses its sympathy. Regarding the above issues, the responsible representatives can be promoted by both labor and capital, and each group can form a joint committee to study and discuss item by item to seek a fair and peaceful solution as a buffer step. The Trade Union representative said that the labor side is also willing to form a joint committee, but the employer must continue to fulfill the substitute system as a prerequisite, otherwise there is no need to talk about anything. Zhang replied that since the union regards the substitute issue as the focus of the solution, he should report it to the association's executive meeting tomorrow, and formally reply to the union after the meeting has made a decision. This was the actual situation of the negotiations at that time, and the reporters from the news agencies also heard it at the scene. It is not allowed to confuse the public. It is only with this that it is closely related to the industry's labor strike this time, so a solemn statement is made.

Reply to the Trade Union To reply directly, I received a letter from your union a few days ago, in which you sent Zhao Zhenhui and other five representatives to the Standing Committee member of our association, Zhang Meian, and requested three items, and asked for a reply. It has been decided by the Executive Committee of our association yesterday that the three requirements put forward by your union are of great importance, and the Executive Committee of our association did not dare to decide without authorization, and intends to submit it to the members' meeting of our association on July 5 for discussion, so as to make specific replies based on public opinion. It is appropriate to send a letter of guarantee. Please check it and hope that your union will adhere to the principle of labor-capital cooperation and the spirit of overcoming difficulties together. Before the members' meeting of our association is convened, do not take any actions that will affect the social illness, which is what we pray for.

The City Party Department's Instructions The City Party Department instructed both parties, "For the purpose of ordering compliance, the report is based on the fact that the labor and capital parties in the pharmaceutical industry have disputes over labor-capital agreements, brewing strikes, and urgently need to find ways to mediate, etc. According to this, the labor-capital agreement of the industry was previously agreed upon and signed by both parties, and approved by the former Civil Training Committee of the association for filing. It should be abided by as a whole. If there are inconsistencies between the agreement and the current laws and regulations that need to be amended, the method drafted by the former Central Training Department should also be followed. The announcement issued jointly by the former Civil Training Committee and the Social Bureau of the association should be followed. The labor and capital parties should sign their opinions and submit them to the party and government agencies for review and revision. The old agreement of the industry has not been amended in accordance with the above methods, and should continue to be effective according to law. No party shall arbitrarily break it or make excessive demands beyond the scope of statutory benefits, causing disputes. According to the previous situation reported, in addition to ordering the industry (Trade Association) (Vocational Trade Union) to comply with it, it is urgently ordered that the association must comply with it strictly and not deliberately violate it. Be sure to order,"

Hill's Waterworks Report 140

The Public Works Department Information Office announced that Hill's report stated that the Review Committee met on June 20. In addition to the report, the opinions of the Finance Director and the Works Director were also presented, as well as a summary by the Chinese members. The main points were that the company should change to silver to calculate its capital. Also, a member stated his opinion that he did not want to criticize Hill's report. However, Hill's stay in Shanghai was short and he could not fully understand the local situation. In his opinion, the estimated amount of domestic water use per person per day in the report was too high. The leakage layer, due to loose joints and evaporation of water, did not seem to be fully included. Also, the company should reduce personnel and save expenses, and the smell of water in certain locations was not up to American standards. Furthermore, for poor users, the water package system should still be used to describe water use for heavy hygiene. The cost of installing water meters universally may not be worth the loss. The chairman of the committee replied that the expert's report did not seem to be easily criticized by outsiders. As for the universal installation of water meters, although the Chinese taxpayers' meeting made such a suggestion, the Public Works Department considered it beneficial. Hill also advocated installing meters without affecting the preferential treatment of poor users. The water quality layer was actually due to the muddy water source, but the company had responded to Hill's suggestion to build a large clear water pool. For the prevention of water leakage, Hill had also made some proposals. After further discussion, the committee suggested Zheng Duan, (1) Hill's report, recognizing the water price as fair and reasonable, and the efficiency of the company's organization and administration at all levels, requested the Board of Directors to accept. The other suggestions of Hill and the additional opinions of the Finance and Works Directors should be negotiated by representatives of the Public Works Department and the company, and special attention should be paid to the following items. (2) Regarding cost savings, personnel from the Public Works Department and the company should negotiate. (3) The company should be urged to continue its current policy of raising capital in silver. (4) In view of the reasons stated by the Finance and Works Directors, the price of fire-fighting water should not be increased. (5) The pricing after the universal installation of water meters should still be particularly preferential to poor and small users. (6) Article 17 of the concession contract, that is, the company's land may not be opened to the estimated price, and the above section may not be changed. The above suggestions have now been adopted by the Board of Directors.
